Remember how he lost his finger because nobody ever showed him the proper blade technique? [emotional] That's why we started all this, right? Because people were getting hurt and, I mean, the old training was basically "here's your hairnet, don't die."

[excited] But now it's like—wait, sorry, I'm getting ahead of myself—but the standardization committee said our injury rates dropped seventy percent! [speeding up] And they want me to present at the conference, and honestly I'm kind of terrified because what if—[trail off]

[warm] No, you know what? This is good. This is really, really good. We're gonna save fingers, er, save lives even. [chuckle] God, I need to call my mom.
711. [confused] Twenty-three percent. That's, um, that's what it says. Twenty-three percent Eastern European. Dad's—I mean, the man I've called Dad for thirty-two years is like, one hundred percent Irish. So that's... [pause] that's not possible, right? Unless—oh God. 

Well, I keep refreshing the page thinking maybe it's, you know, some kind of error. But it's not changing. [shaky voice] The thing is, Mom always said I had his eyes. Actually, everyone said that. "You look just like your father." Hmm, which father though, right? 

I guess I should—I don't even know what I should do. [cry] Call Mom? Basically demand she explain why she's been lying to me my entire life? Or, er, maybe she thought I knew? No, that's—that's ridiculous. 

[bitter] You know what's funny? I spent literally years defending him when people said we looked nothing alike. [whispering] "Genetics are weird," I'd say. Yeah, turns out they're pretty straightforward actually.

So now what? I mean, do I tell him? [anxious] Does he know? Has he always known? The thing is, he taught me to ride a bike, walked me down the aisle, held my daughter when she was born. [long pause] That's still real, right? Like, that happened. 

[very quietly] I just... I don't know who I am anymore.
712. Twenty-three years I've been at that plant. Twenty-three. [bitter] And for what, honestly? We organized, we—I mean, we really thought the union would actually back us this time. [frustrated] Like, we had the votes, you know? Everyone signed those cards, um, everyone showed up to the meetings even though they were scared. 

[sigh] Martinez got fired first, then basically half of second shift. And what did our rep say? [mocking] "We need to follow proper channels." Proper channels while, uh, while people are losing their houses? [angry] I can't even look at Rodriguez anymore, I told him—no wait, I promised him—that if we stuck together, err, if we all just stayed united... 

[very sad] His kid's got medical bills, and I stood there telling him the union would protect us. [pause] The thing is, I really believed it, you know? Like an idiot, I guess. [quietly] All those nights organizing, and then corporate just... they didn't even negotiate. Just pink slips. Done.

[exhausted] So now what, right? I'm fifty-two, and suddenly I'm supposed to just, what, start over? [bitter] "Retraining opportunities," they said. [laugh] Yeah, okay. Retraining for what exactly? [trailing off] I don't even know anymore...
713. [upset] बीस घंटे। वो मुझे हफ्ते में बीस घंटे दे रहे हैं—ये, अम्म, ये literally आधा है जितना मैं काम करता था। [frustrated] Christmas से ठीक पहले, मेरा मतलब, seriously? कौन करता है ऐसा? [pause] मैं वहां कितने, अ, करीब दो साल से हूं, और ये लोग—[bitter] "slow season" मेरी जूती। ये bakery है यार! लोग holidays में cookies और cakes खरीदते हैं ना?

[anxious] तो अब मैं क्या करूं, जैसे, आधी salary से rent कैसे दूं? और मैंने अपनी भांजी से कहा था कि मैं उसे वो, अ, वो art set दिलाऊंगा, [sad] महंगा वाला जिसमें सारे markers और... [sigh] हे भगवान, पता नहीं यार।

[angry] पता है क्या बात सबसे ज्यादा खराब लगती है? उन्होंने पिछले महीने दो नए लोग रखे। दो! और somehow मेरे घंटे काट रहे हैं? [shaky voice] मैं बस—मुझे सच में समझ नहीं आ रहा ये legal कैसे है।

[long pause]

[exhausted] शायद मुझे, जैसे, कुछ और ढूंढना शुरू करना चाहिए। कोई second job या, पता नहीं, बिल्कुल नई job ही। [very quietly] बात ये है कि मुझे वहां काम करना actually अच्छा लगता था। [sniffle] सुबह ताज़ी bread की खुशबू, regular customers जो मेरा नाम जानते थे... [trailing off]

[determined] खैर। मैं कुछ न कुछ figure out कर लूंगा। हमेशा करता ही हूं ना।
